< review>
On the way in Salinas to a Subway, we saw this little cafe and promptly stopped. And we were right! The cafe has an inviting interior. But that's not all. We had a small cup of clamp chowder comparable to clamp chowders at other places. Then we had sandwiches: there's many options on the menu and we ordered different sandwiches. All were of excellent quality and very very tasty. The price is absolutely comparable to other lunchrooms.<//review>

With all the fuss that I have heard about Cream, it took me almost four years before I finally had my first.

Things to know,

It is now $4 for one ice cream sandwich and one topping is no longer included (will cost you $.75 each)
You can mix and match your cookies before they warm in the oven + 1 one ice cream choice
Suggest you split in half and share unless you have a huge sweet tooth

Overall Thoughts

While I am glad to have finally tried Cream, I do not forsee myself going back especially if there is a line</Text>

I wouldn't wait in a long line for this, but I do love ice cream, so I might wander back in here sometime again.< /text>

<text>You know that irresistible aroma of fresh-baked cookies that flows in the air and wafts past your nose making you stop in your step and wonder, "where is that delicious scent coming from?" Yea, that's how Cream entices you into their store. I was able to resist the first time I came to the area, just buying Gong Cha and leaving. But when I came with my family, my sister was unable to resist the tempting aroma of cookies and made it her mission to get an ice cream sandwich cookie before we headed back to LA. And I followed her inside since the smell of cookies was just too amazing.

So Cream has a wide assortment of freshly baked cookies as well as a good number of ice cream flavors and toppings to do any sort of combination/creation that your heart desires. You can get cookies by itself, ice cream by itself, make an ice cream cookie sandwich, add toppings, make a premium ice cream cookie sandwich, make sundaes, make a taco (3 ice cream flavors and 2 toppings), purchase brownies, buy milkshakes, or get a coffee drink. Yep, the menu is pretty extensive. So if you want to make some sort of ice cream cookie concoction, chances are the workers at Cream will help you out.

I tried the butter sugar cookie on its own while my sister got a snickerdoodle salted caramel ice cream sandwich. The cookies individually weren't too expensive - like around a dollar or so for each, and they were taken right out of the oven! The butter sugar cookie was a bit of a let down in that it was way too sweet. I couldn't finish the entire cookie because the flavor was a bit too cloying. It reminded me a lot of the sugar cookies from Ralph's, which .. meh, are decent but not the best.

The moment I heard my sister order the ice cream sandwich, I knew she wouldn't finish it. And I was right! The combination was way too sweet. The snickerdoodle cookies were amazing. Still warm from the oven, it tasted like cinnamon and sugar - bliss! The salted caramel ice cream was also good - by itself. It's definitely nowhere near as good as Bi-Rite's. Mixed with the cookie and it was really sweet. And I like sweet things, but this was too much. We couldn't finish the cookie sandwich and had to toss some of it in the trash, which was really sad. However, price for this wasn't too bad - around $3-$4 and I think there was a check in offer.

tl;dr - Workers are fairly nice. This shop is definitely a good place to go if you're in the mood for a quick dessert or treat. Everything is clean, there are plenty of tables, the storefront is amazing, and the smell of cookies will draw you in! I would recommend trying the flavors of ice cream first before combining it with a cookie because these concoctions can get super sweet! I would just order cookies and ice cream separately, but that's just me. Glad I got to try Cream and it's good to know that there are locations in SoCal that I can easily visit. I rarely get a craving for ice cream, so if anything I will be back for the cookies!<//text></record>

< text>
Urgent Care Review:  Short version:  Patient care was their priority, not numbers or computer systems.

I took my wife who was very ill on a Wednesday morning.  First time patient there, front office staff were very helpful with what to fill out.  Paperwork to fill out was minimal for a first time visit (took less than 3 minutes).  Asked if we could get her in a room early so she could lie down, which they accommodated given the reason for visit.  (Most places wouldn't do this).  The RN or CNA who drew her blood hit the vein on the first try, on my severely dehydrated wife, who has rolling veins (Amazing!).  The next RN or CNA noticed that the IV they added was leaking very slightly, and took the time to test multiple parts on the line to find the leak, and fix it.  The PA came in and went through the possibilities of what it was, and sent us on our way to a radiology site nearby to get imaging done.  Results of bloodwork and imaging were done within 2 hours of leaving, and it took a simple call to get the results.  When I called, they put the PA that saw my wife on the phone to tell me the results.

Out of all of the urgent cares I've gone to in my life, this was the best.  Thank you all.<//text>

<text>I found Dr. Wong through my dental care provider but I couldn't be happier with my decision!

First--location. His practice is located in a really convenient area, relatively close to BART (so close to your commute), with sufficient parking.

Second--service. His staff members are super nice and accommodating. When I brought my then 1 yr old daughter for her 'happy' appointment, they made her feel comfortable and welcome considering how scared kids can be at that age.

Third--work. I don't know how many teeth fillings he had to do but it was a lot (I had three separate appointments and was there about 1.5 hours each time) and so far everything is great. <user_id>112492086154402357350< /user_id><username>Jonathan Dirrenberger</username><Date>1615273537584< /Date>< Rate>
3< /Rate>
<review>This playground is great for kids 3 and under. It's okay for kids older than that. The main equipment is basically one long, elevated platform with little "towers" every 30 ft or so that get progressively higher off the ground with a covered slide at the end. Each tower has different ways to climb up/down it like rope ladders, poles, etc. There is a semi-circle device that is basically a modern version of a teeter totter and probably was once pretty great, but it's so weathered and worn that there is too much friction for it to be much fun for any kid under about 10 (and how many kids that age come here?!). There is a zip line, though it's the sanitized version where it's on a metal track and very short with hardly any elevation change so pretty lackluster. There are toddler/baby swings as well as 2 regular swings and a merry-go-round with rope tower; all pretty standard playground stiff. There is a little climbing wall that uses actual faux rock instead of holds, but I have no idea who the target audience is because it's way too hard for any kid who would be of the age that they would be coming to this program.

Finally, this playground has an interesting vibe because it's buried behind houses and hence removed from a road which makes it somewhat peaceful. It's also basically built into the side of a steep hill, so one side effectively has a wall of earth (with lots of plants and stairs up to the Rec Center).

Overall, this is a pretty average park in a neighborhood, St. Mary's Park, that not many people visit or know about, so worth  checking out if you're not from the immediate area as a way to try a new playground with the kids.<//review><pictures>None< /pictures><resp>None< /resp>< gmapID>

Overpriced and rude staff.
Placed a togo order for pick up around 5 o'clock p.m. On a Friday night for 2 burritos with only beans cheese rice and sour cream, one burrito with only beans cheese and rice and a bowl of tortilla soup . When we picked it up the order came to $38 for 3 tiny burrito's (that didn't even fill up one to go container) and a small to go cup of chicken broth maybe half a cup of shredded chicken and some soggy chips. When I expressed my disappointment that they charge $10 for a small burrito with only beans cheese rice and sour cream the manager got defensive and said they only have one size burrito eith an excuse that they are not a taqueria so their burritos aren't big. I told him for the price and the size that that is ridiculous and he said "no its not" arguing with me the whole-time. I explained to him that I could go to restaurants like La Villa or Jorge's el Tapatio right down the street places that are also "not taquerias" and get gigantic burrito's for that price and $9 for a small cup of soup with only broth shredded chicken and soggy chips, No avacado, no cheese (To their defense I asked for no pico de gallo) is overpriced. I got my money back and I went to Jorge's  el tapatio and got the same order but with pozole instead of tortilla soup (they dont have tortilla soup) and got way more food for $7 less . I will try to attach pictures so I don't just sound crazy in the picture of casa grande I dumped the soup into a bowl so that you could see it. < Text>
Basic Denny's visit except handicap access.  Great biscuits!  Standard menu offerings.  Adequate, filling and reasonably priced.  Apparent retrofit for handicap access.  Smooth path from parking area to entry at side front of building.  Narrow path from entry lobby to restaurant due to large claw game to get stuffed animals that juts into travel path.  Once inside, adequate access to table/seating.  Path to bathrooms difficult with 3 sharp right angles and minimal space to manuever.  First right angle at top of stairs, limited room to turn w/c to get into BR hallway.  In short hallway, sharp angle to left then sharp right into ladies BR.  Men's BR did not have access sign.  Husband helped me negotiate turns with difficulty.  Once inside the larger of the two stalls, not enough room to back in to transfer, coming in straight kept door open with attendant on outside of stall.  One of the most challenging BRs I've used since being w/c bound.  Good hand washing access!  Same struggles getting back out of the BR and hallway.  Kudos to cashier for offering to assist me. That was so very kind.  I declined as with family who helped.  I don't think I could have managed as a solo traveler.< /Text>

< Review>
I visit this place occasionally, usually late at night or early morning when nothing else is open, and I usually have a pretty good experience. The food is up to par, and the waitstaff is amiable. However, I just had such a negative experience with one waiter that I won't be going back. I would rather get chips and a soda at a 7/11 than go back.
My Fiancee and I went there around 11:00 PM Christmas evening. There were a fair few people in there, and our server, Laurance, was serving at least three tables. Now, I totally understand exactly how much it sucks to work on Christmas. I know how much it sucks to work night shifts, I know how much low wage work sucks and I know what it feels like to have way too much work on your plate. But this guy's attitude was so bad I wanted to walk out of there as soon as he brought us our water. My Fiancee convinced me to stay, and we ordered our food and ate, and the bad attitude persisted. I almost left him a tip and a note saying something to the effect of "I understand that this is a bad day for you," but he just got worse as the night progressed, so we paid and left. I have an emotional disorder and I've had really bad days at work. But you NEVER treat customers that way.<//Review>
